Free Talk

On Literature 306

— Wu Xi

Some say, "Truly powerful literary works should be like mellow wine, easy to drink."

I cannot agree with this statement.

What constitutes a literary work? It is not determined by whether it is "mellow" or "extremely strong" to drink, but by the work's artistic merit: this is what I think.

For example, a piece of writing called a literary work might have a "sword-drawn-and-bow-bent" form, but lacks the "sword-drawn-and-bow-bent" content. This cannot be considered a "truly powerful literary work." If it has content and a form suitable for the content, but lacks artistic value – perhaps just a collection of new terms and slogans, or merely a description of concepts – it cannot be considered "art." If it is indeed artistic, even though it is "extremely strong" both when drinking and after, can we exclude it from the realm of art, using the condition of "not mellow to drink" to deny its existence as a "literary work"?

Conversely, just because it is "mellow to drink" does not necessarily mean it is a "truly powerful literary work," and it might "intoxicate you to death later on." We must also consider the artistic value of this "mellow wine." "The subject matter is just a simple story" – that is, of course, not a problem. However, even if the subject matter is not simple, but it is real: perhaps an accidental material, but this accident reveals necessity: can such a subject matter not be taken up? Moreover, even if it is "mellow to drink" and then "intoxicating," is this "intoxication" due to the fragrance of the wine, or due to the toxins contained within fermenting? Our literary theorists cannot but pay attention to this, right? However, this is beyond the scope of the current topic.

Therefore, I say, "truly powerful literary works" should be viewed from the perspective of the work's artistic merit. Placing the focus of investigation on whether it is "mellow" or not "mellow" to drink will not only make people "confused" but also lead them to repeat old "wrong paths."

"But it is not to say that literary works that are extremely strong to drink are not wanted. However, writers should not be satisfied with just being strong to drink." Although the wording is tactful, it actually denies the existence of the former.

Who has ever said that literary works only need to be "active," "sharp," and "stimulating" in "words"?

Reading Yan's Family Instructions 307

— Xu Maoyong

When Liang Qichao and Mr. Hu Shih were compiling lists of books that scholars of Chinese studies must read, I was only fourteen or fifteen years old. For some reason, I originally had a strong ambition to study Chinese studies, but when I saw those lists, I was intimidated and gave up on Chinese studies altogether. I only randomly read a few collections of poems and prose from those lists, hoping to gain some benefit in writing. As for Song and Ming Neo-Confucianism and other books on moral cultivation, I didn't read a single one.

Now it seems that I am not alone. In general, young people almost entirely focus on writing and neglect morality in terms of cultivation. Therefore, people's hearts are not as they used to be, and young people are becoming increasingly frivolous, especially those who write, most of them often lack kindness. Recently, someone has proposed moral cultivation for young people and recommended good books as the foundation for cultivation, which I think is a very meaningful thing. This is much more important than the issue of how to cultivate oneself in literature, which was proposed at the same time. At least for myself, I feel the need to read these good books. However, I have flipped through the "Analects" and "Mencius" before, but not as moral books. Only "Yan's Family Instructions" has always made me hesitate because of the words "family instructions," so I have never read it. Now I want to read it, and I have to start with this book.

After reading it, I have certainly benefited a lot in terms of morality丨but I still have to wait until I can follow the instructions and put them into practice丨but at the same time, I discovered a contradiction that made me feel bewildered. Originally, I am someone who still wants to write, and the reason why I want to cultivate morality at the same time is to do both, to "accumulate morality" and to "be able to write." However, according to the examples given by Yan, "literati have always been prone to frivolity." There is often a contradiction between writing and morality. He said: "Qu Yuan exposed his talent and praised himself, revealing the faults of the ruler; Song Yu's appearance was seductive, seen as an actor; Dongfang Manqian was humorous and vulgar; Sima Xiangru stole wealth and had no integrity; Wang Bao exaggerated his virtues; Yang Xiong's virtue was defeated by his beautiful new style; Li Ling surrendered to the barbarians; Liu Xin betrayed the Han dynasty; Fu Yi was a partisan of powerful families; Ban Gu stole his father's history; Zhao Yuanshu's resistance was excessive; Feng Jingtong was frivolous and extravagant; Ma Jichang was flattering and received ridicule; Cai Yong shared the same evil and was executed; Wu Zhi criticized his hometown; Cao Zhi was arrogant and violated the law; Du Du asked for leave without satisfaction; Lu Cui was extremely narrow-minded; Chen Lin was truly crude and careless; Fan Qin had no self-control; Liu Zhen was forced to work as a laborer; Wang Can was impatient and disliked; Kong Rong and Mi Heng were arrogant and led to their downfall; Yang Xiu and Ding Yi stirred up trouble and were killed; Ruan Ji was impolite and corrupted customs; Ji Kang was arrogant and met a violent end; Fu Xuan was dismissed from office for fighting; Sun Chu was arrogant and disrespectful; Lu Ji rebelled and took risks; Pan Yue spoke empty words and courted danger; Yan Yannian was stubborn and dismissed; Xie Lingyun was empty and disorderly; Wang Yuanzhang was a fierce bandit who brought disaster upon himself; Xie Xuanhui was insulting and was punished…" Even the likes of Ziyou, Zixia, Xun Kuang, and Mencius… were also said by Yan to have "caused more harm than good."

Looking at the names listed above, most of them are important authors in the "Selections of Refined Literature." If their works were removed, the "Selections of Refined Literature" would lose its value for recommending to young literary enthusiasts. However, from a moral point of view, they are worthless. Even Mencius, who wrote "Mencius," is not accepted by moralists. Therefore, is there not only a contradiction between literature and morality, but also a contradiction between morality and morality?

Confucius must have been the most moral, but he had no writing. Yan himself also has literary works, but they are not considered outstanding when included in the "Selections of Refined Literature." Who is the perfect person who "accumulates morality and is able to write"? Is it only Ouyang Wenzhong Gong? However, the poem "Willow of Jiangnan" was also suspected of "stealing from his nephew," and was slandered by Qian Mufu. This really makes us young people with aspirations for cultivation wonder where to go.

Yan explained the reason why literati are prone to destruction, saying: "The nature of writing emphasizes excitement and expresses spirituality, making people arrogant, so they neglect self-control and are eager to advance. This is an increasingly serious problem for contemporary literati… Moreover, the injuries caused by slander are worse than those caused by spears and halberds, and the disasters of satire are faster than the wind." This is indeed very true. On this point, we should strictly abide by Yan's instructions: "It is advisable to be deeply cautious to preserve good fortune." (The above original texts are all from the "On Writing" chapter)

Not only are there contradictions between morality and writing, and between morality and morality, but there are also contradictions between writing and writing. For example, the "Encouraging Learning" chapter says:

"There was a powerful official who misread the Shu Capital Rhapsody, annotating: 'Dun Chi' is taro. This is because it looks like the character for sheep. Someone gave him mutton, and he replied in a letter, 'Thank you for the donation of Dun Chi,' which shocked the entire court, who did not understand the meaning. Only after a long time of investigation did they realize this."

This anecdote is actually caused by too much literary cultivation. If it were an ordinary person, they would simply say "Thank you for the donation of mutton." Although it would show a lack of vocabulary, it would certainly not cause "the entire court to be shocked and not understand the meaning." The instructors might say, "That's because he read the wrong version of the Shu Capital Rhapsody!" However, who can guarantee that the "Selections of Refined Literature" does not have any wrong versions?

Pier 308

— Xu Zhuanpeng

When there is no headwind, the pier boat arrives at a fixed time upstream. Every day, just as the city lights up, the pier boat blows its conch shell to dock.

Today, from morning till dusk, it has been raining, and a strong north wind has been blowing. The weather is gloomy and terribly cold, as if snow is about to fall. It is already past 9 PM, but the boat has not yet arrived.

The pier coolies and innkeepers are hiding in small bars and teahouses, waiting for the passengers from the boat. The cold compels them to breathe out misty air, and their teeth are chattering. They want to drink a sip of hot wine or hot tea to increase their body temperature. They constantly approach the window facing the river to look at the dark river surface. There is a spark of fire, sometimes red, sometimes black. It gradually moves forward, and it also seems to gradually retreat… Someone's shouts can be faintly heard on the beach.

"Those are the boatmen!"

Someone asks, "Have you seen the boat?"

The reply is, "I've seen the boat's lights."

So someone says in a seemingly happy voice, "Then the boat will arrive soon."

Another group of poorer coolies who are not qualified to enter the bars and teahouses to avoid the wind are gathered in a corner where the wind cannot reach, burning a pile of garbage. Each of them has dreamy eyes.

It is already past 11 PM in the city, and they look at the river again. The boat's lights seem to be still in the same place. But the torches lit by the boatmen on the beach can be seen very clearly.

"The boat is coming soon," someone says again.

"It looks very close, but it will take at least an hour. With such a strong wind, the boat is also blown back…"

The small city is completely asleep. The boat's conch shell blows loudly in the dead of night. The boat finally docks.

The various bars and snack shops along the pier turn on their oil lamps, waiting for the "hungry" customers who come down from the boat.

The innkeepers and coolies, with their hazy, dreamy eyes wide open, rush out and crowd onto the pier.

But what comes out of the cabin is a group of "broke" people. They have no luggage other than a small package. These are people who do not need coolies and are not worth the "greeting" of innkeepers! Who would be willing to go out in such bad weather if they had money? The coolies and innkeepers quietly disperse with disappointed hearts.

The boatmen come ashore and barge into the bar. Their faces are swollen from the wind and appear brownish. Wet footprints are scattered on the floor, and their feet are completely white from being soaked in water.

The bar owner, who is used to saying nice things:

"Poor you, having to be barefoot in the water in such cold weather…"

The boatmen seem to be comforted: "Only you pity us, boss lady. Quickly get us a pound of wine, scalding hot…"

They drink, drink, and call for more until the second half of the night, when the bar owner dozes off on the counter. The boatmen stagger out drunkenly.

"Boss lady, put it on my tab, I didn't bring any cash!"

She reluctantly utters an "oh" sound. She seems to have guessed that the boatmen had no cash. She closes the bar door and thinks that she is not happy to open the door again tomorrow. She feels that running a small bar is not the way out…

Reader's Letter 309

Brother Lie Wen:

Today, I saw Mr. Qi Ying's article "Chaliapin and Gorky." The Chaliapin story he remembers is something I didn't know. I once read his autobiography published in 1927. In that book, he didn't mention his unwillingness to return to his homeland, but he said that his "escape" from his homeland was because he had stayed in his homeland for too long and was afraid that the European art world would forget him. Therefore, with the help of Lunacharsky, he left his homeland on Li Lie Weizhi's special train. Without the description in Mr. Qi Ying's book "Masks and People," we would have been easily deceived by him. Now, judging from Mr. Qi Ying's writing, this Mr. Chaliapin did have a somewhat "slippery" attitude towards his homeland after the revolution. His homeland did not abandon him, but he abandoned his homeland first, which is not commendable.

I am unwilling to distort a worshiper of the aristocracy as a free man of art for the sake of praising art, so please publish this letter in "Free Talk" to show the readers and Mr. Qi Ying. Shi Zhecun

Two Brothers (6) (8) 310

— Guy de Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

He was gripped by a sudden terror, which came so quickly and authoritatively that it was as if he had burst into his bedroom without even opening the door.

The room seemed empty. Only a candle on the wardrobe illuminated the room.

Jean ran to the window, which was closed, even the shutters were closed. He turned around and searched the dark corners of the room with his panicked gaze. Then he saw that the curtains on the bed had been lowered. He rushed to lift them. His mother was sleeping in his bed, her face buried in the pillow, which she had grabbed with her spasmodic hands and placed on her head so as not to hear anything anymore.

At first, he thought she was suffocating. Then he grabbed her shoulder and turned her over. She still hadn't abandoned the pillow that covered her face, which she was biting with her mouth to avoid crying out.

But as soon as he touched this stiff body, these two spasmodic arms, he understood the indescribable pain she had suffered. Watching her use her hands and teeth so resolutely and forcefully to stuff the feather-filled bag into her mouth, covering her ears and eyes, so that he couldn't see her or talk to her, he knew from the blow he himself had suffered how much pain one could endure. Then his heart, his simple heart, was overwhelmed with pity. He was not a judge, not even a merciful judge, he was only a weak person, a gentle son. He didn't remember anything else she had said to him. He didn't investigate or argue. He just touched his mother's motionless body with her hands. Unable to take the pillow off her face, he kissed her clothes and cried:

"Mom, Mom, my poor Mom, look at me!"

She would have been dead if a barely visible shiver, a vibration of a taut string, hadn't run through her body. He said repeatedly:

"Mom, Mom, listen to me, this is not true. I know this is not true."

She twitched, choked, and then suddenly sobbed on the pillow. Then all her nerves relaxed. Her stiff muscles softened, and her half-open fingers released the pillow. He discovered her tearful face.

Her face was completely white, and tears streamed from her closed eyelids. He hugged her neck, kissed her eyes, kissed her slowly, frantically, and forcefully, his lips soaked with her tears. He kept saying:

"Mom, dear Mom, I know this is not true. Don't cry, I know! This is not true!"

She sat up, staring at him, and said to him with the courage needed to commit suicide in certain situations:

"You're wrong, it's true, my child."

Then there was silence between them. For a moment, she choked again. She straightened her throat and tilted her head back to breathe. Then she overcame herself again and said:

"It's true, my child. Why would I lie? It's true. If I lied, you wouldn't believe it."

Securities Market: Except for Swap Transactions, Bond Market Sees Very Little New Trading 316

Prices of various bonds fluctuate slightly with swap transactions.

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange saw a relatively stable market. Except for swap transactions, there was very little new trading. Market prices fluctuated, slightly rising or falling depending on whether long or short positions were being swapped. Regarding the overall situation, although the conflict between Fujian and Zhejiang has made contact, both long and short sides remain in a wait-and-see attitude, hoping for future victory, and are mutually persistent. Therefore, the market is calm. Long positions are more common in swaps, and market prices are slightly weak. However, the trend remained strong at the close. At the opening in the morning, short swaps saw a difference of 2 yuan between near-term and distant terms for treasury bonds. Salt tax and other near-term and distant terms differed by 1 yuan for most. Market prices for treasury bonds were slightly better at 19 customs gold by 1-2 jiao, while the rest all returned slightly by 1-4 jiao. In the second session, long swaps were appropriate, and various groups sold this month and bought distant terms, and the market price showed a phenomenon of near-term weakness and distant-term strength. The trend still appeared slightly weak. The market opened in the afternoon with still many short swaps. Except for a slight increase of 0.15 jiao for the unified tax, the rest all returned 1-2 jiao. There were very few closing transactions, with only some settlement transactions on the surface. Front prices were slightly lower, while rear prices were stronger. The overall situation for the day showed no clear trend. Because both long and short swaps have considerable limitations, there were no major increases or decreases in trading. In the end, the prices of two or three varieties for the current month were slightly better by 1 jiao, while the rest were all down slightly by 1-5 jiao. In general, near-term was stronger than distant-term. The total transaction volume was 15.48 million yuan, including 5,000 yuan in spot goods, 5.75 million in unified salt tax futures, 3.09 million in treasury bonds, 1.48 million in 19 customs gold, 2.33 million in 20 bonds of 20 customs, and the rest ranging from tens of thousands to 3-500,000 yuan. US Cotton Awaits Commercial Development 325

▲ Trading is Slack Due to Holidays

A report from New York on the 22nd regarding the cotton market for the week states that the cotton market was limited last week due to the approaching holidays, and most of the trading was for the near term. The long positions for December and January were mostly swapped to distant terms. There was very little selling in the South. The increase in spot goods traditionally given before the holidays has not materialized, reportedly because most cotton farmers have accepted a deposit of 1 jiao. Although business has improved somewhat, it is limited by the uncertainty of the future of the gold standard. The dispute over the reduction of cotton fields in 1934 will begin soon, and the results will be decided at the end of January. People in the industry are waiting for a turnaround in commerce and the performance of the next crop. The basic commodity market is quiet and firm, also hoping for a revival of demand in the new year.

Grains: Large Quantities of American Flour Reportedly Being Shipped 326

| Standard Flour Weakens Again |

Yesterday, the flour market initially rose, then fell, and finally weakened again. In the morning, the market sentiment was very good because the American telegram reported that wheat futures rose by 1 yuan. Factories covered positions, and all months remained firm. In the afternoon, it was rumored in the market that flour accounted for 4/10 of the wheat that was borrowed and that it would be gradually shipped to Shanghai for sale. The actual sales of flour in the Shanghai market are not strong. With large quantities of American flour arriving in Shanghai, the market must fall further. Therefore, domestic buyers have no business sense. However, factories are not selling off and have even taken advantage of small covering positions, slightly holding up the market. However, actual sales and customer hoarding are not interested, so the market is still trending downward. Therefore, January is down by 0.015 yuan, February is down by 0.0125 yuan, April and May are down by 0.01 yuan each, March is down by 0.0075 yuan, and the current month is also down by 0.0025 yuan.

Trading of Futures Wheat is Quiet 327

Yesterday, the wheat market was quiet in both the morning and afternoon, and there were few transactions throughout the day. Factories were watching, and speculative traders did not sell, with both sides sticking to their positions, waiting for opportunities. However, foreign wheat telegrams reported an increase of more than 1 yuan. New foreign wheat has not been unloaded because the issue of tax exemption has not been resolved, so standard wheat has temporarily returned to flat. The closing price was 0.01 yuan higher for January and 0.01 yuan lower for February, March, and April. Since the new foreign wheat has not been unloaded from the docks, spot wheat in the market has turned around. Yesterday, Shen Da shipped two small cars of Haizhou wheat and Dali Ji wheat, priced at 4.09 yuan to 4.05 yuan, which was also several points better than the previous market.

White Tung Oil Market in Hankou is Slightly Better 333

Therefore, Hankou merchants and foreign firms are shipping out as soon as they are approved, and there seems to be no chance to see. Zhejiang tung is somewhat similar and slightly better, but it is unexpected that the situation on the Zhejiang border is tight again, and it is inevitable that it will be slightly hit. ▲ American Sales of Dry Warp Stop: American sales of Lyons warp have plummeted. Local American merchants have been rarely throwing money for dry warp purchases. Shipments to the United States have stopped. No dry warp was shipped to American territories last week, but 75 packages were shipped to Europe and Asia.

Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Cafe

The Conflict Between Brains and Bellies 354

— Yi

In these turbulent times, any young person unwilling to be left behind wants to diligently pursue education and fill their mind. But to achieve this goal, a problem must first be solved: finding a way to keep the belly from being empty, because an empty, hungry belly makes learning impossible. However, in this day and age, unless one has vast family wealth, avoiding the danger of an empty belly—solving the problem of livelihood—is no easy task. Even if one is fortunate enough to find a job that keeps the belly full and in a normal state, it is impossible to simultaneously concentrate on studying and filling the mind. With the unemployment crisis growing, job sectors are overcrowded and working hours are increasing. If you are lucky enough to find a job, besides the time spent working and socializing to keep it, can you still find free time to study? From this, it is clear that one cannot cater to the belly and the brain at the same time; if one wants to cater to the brain, one cannot cater to the belly: the two are in conflict at present.

We often see in classified ads in newspapers that many young people are looking for jobs, some hoping to achieve the goal of working part-time and studying part-time. This clearly shows that, under the two great desires of survival and knowledge, they want to eliminate the conflict between belly and brain, and want to nourish both at the same time. But the reality tells us that most of these young people hoping to work and study fail, and some even face the danger of going hungry. Of course, among those hoping to work and study, some do achieve their goals, but even if they fully succeed, in reality they only achieve "half-study," still failing to satisfy their desire for knowledge. Therefore, survival and knowledge, these two great desires, are currently unfulfilled for most young people. The conflict between belly and brain is irreconcilable for most young people in the current situation.

Survival is certainly more important than knowledge. When young people cannot afford to nourish both belly and brain at the same time, they have no choice but to strive for the sake of the belly. As a result, the struggle for human survival becomes more acute, and the many absurd, despicable, and cruel phenomena produced in this struggle increase daily. Whose fault is this? Who should be responsible for this? I say: from the conflict between belly and brain existing in the average young person, to their abandonment of the brain and sole focus on the belly, all these phenomena are caused by "poverty" under the current social system.

Life

Little Master Gets a Haircut 355

— Bi

Apprentice

Heavens! You're deliberately going against me, making my hair grow so fast: long and fluffy, looking like…a mess, really ugly.

The hair just keeps growing, but my pockets don't grow a single copper. What can I do? Just let it grow forever!

My neck is strained and sore. I've been eagerly waiting until the fifteenth, rushing to collect my wages—a colorful banknote. Don't misunderstand; it's not a hundred-yuan bill, or even ten or five, but a one-yuan bill. Ha! How amusing! Stuffed in my pocket, it makes my chest puff out a bit.

Hair is long, nothing to be done. I have to visit the barbershop. A perfectly good banknote disappears into the tobacconist's counter, turning into six double-dime coins and a dozen coppers. I keep looking around on the way, wondering which barbershop is more economical. Slowly walking to the bridge at the Tianhou Temple, I glimpse a barbershop by the roadside, but the magnificent decoration at the entrance scares me off. Let's go; this isn't my destination.

I can't find one by going further. I have no choice but to go back to that barbershop to check the price list. It probably won't be too

Page 19

expensive! So I returned along the same route. When I arrived at the barbershop, the gold-lettered sign "×××" caught my eye, but I couldn't find the price list. "Let's see what the interior looks like first," I thought.

"Hey! Come in, sit inside." I had barely poked my head in when they greeted me with civilized kidnapping, forcing me to bite the bullet and go in, then figure it out. Wow! Look at the dazzling electric lights, the shiny floors, electric blow-dryers, face massages, and some other unnameable gadgets. The aroma is as strong as the stench in a toilet. Those getting haircuts are pot-bellied gentlemen, smartly dressed young men... The attendants are solicitous, offering tea, wiping hats... I feel like Grandma Liu entering the Grand View Garden, embarrassed to the extreme, my face burning, my heart uneasy, just beating irregularly.

"Little master, what style of haircut?"

"Rounded top, just so-so, quick..." I touched the six double-dime coins in my pocket, really worried: "If he wants more than a yuan, I'm in trouble. Bad luck running into this place. If I tell him to do it just so-so, maybe he'll charge less?"

"Ha! Just so-so..." He spoke to someone else in a Jiangbei accent, the rest of the words unclear. At the same time, he gave a sinister smile that stabbed my weak soul. My already uneasy heart, further stimulated, beat almost abnormally, my breathing seemed difficult, my head was dizzy, my face burning. Ah! I can't take it. I really want to run away.

How anxious my heart is! Touching the six double-dimes in my pocket, I really resent myself, banging my head, wondering how I ended up here. I hesitated: should I give him twenty cents, or forty, or sixty...? Thinking about giving him more, I really don't want to; a month's hard work, only exchanged for a yuan. Giving him less, what if he makes it difficult for me? Finally, my head was cut. I finally decided to take out twenty cents. My hands were shaking, and all the blood in my body seemed to return to my heart at once. Without looking back, I ran away in a puff of smoke. On the road, I took a deep breath, touched the silver coins in my pocket, and couldn't help but laugh a little.

After Having a Family 356

— Jin Yizhai

Electrician

Electricians in China today are considered to be among the better-paid workers. They only work eight hours a day, and the average monthly salary is thirty yuan. They also have regular holidays on Sundays, and I am such a worker. In China's labor force today, I can be considered one of the luckiest. But precisely because of this, my problem arises under these circumstances. At first, because my livelihood was guaranteed, I felt comforted. Also, because of the novelty of the environment, my spirits were maintained, so every day going to and from work, eating at the mess hall, going home to sleep, and sleeping in a bit on Sunday mornings before whiling away the day—this monotonous, mechanical life didn't feel bitter. Unexpectedly, after two or three months, as I met more friends, the situation changed. Seeing the joy of those with families, comforting each other, I felt very envious. At twenty-four, the prime of youth, and with a relatively stable life, I naturally couldn't escape the universal rule of "food and sex." This aroused another kind of need in my spirit and body, making me feel often depressed. However, poaching, visiting prostitutes, and the syphilis specimens in the windows of VD clinics had already scared away my courage. So I focused my thoughts on solving the problem entirely on getting married. Once I had this idea in mind, my spirit changed immediately. When eating at the mess hall, I thought, if I had a wife, I could cook my own meals. Two people cooking for themselves wouldn't necessarily be more expensive than one person eating at the mess hall. When going home to sleep, I thought, isn't living alone in a room the same as living with two people? If I had a wife, I definitely wouldn't have to work so hard and not even have someone to talk to, which is so desolate! Moreover, having a wife can save on laundry and sewing expenses, and it doesn't necessarily increase the burden one-sidedly. Especially on Sundays, those short-lived Sundays, I'm so bored at home. Seeing the strange sights of men and women on the streets of Shanghai, which everyone can see, makes me even more uneasy. At this point, I really think about getting married all the time. What stimulated me the most to make a decision was the difficulty of asking the landlord to open the door when I came home late after playing with friends. He clearly heard me, but pretended not to, making me wait at least half an hour. When he finally opened the door, his unhappy face and the rambling idle talk in his mouth were really unbearable. Then I thought, if I had a wife, I wouldn't be like this!

Now I have a wife! And I have a child! But the happiness is not as I imagined in the past. On the contrary, I feel a new kind of pain. Every time I work, I think about how dangerous it is to play with electricity. If I die because of it, and my wife is tied down by the child and can't work, how will they live? Rely on the compensation? It's very limited, and the capitalists are trying to get rid of it. Every time I come home from work, my body is extremely tired, and I easily get annoyed. But my wife is also tired from household chores and piecework she does at home brought in by others. Her mood may not be good either. So, for her to cook, I have to hold the baby, or if the baby happens to be asleep and she's cooking, I have to fetch things and put them away. In this process, if I slack off a little or do it a little slower, she'll scold me, I'll say something back to her, and we'll start arguing. At this time, I have this feeling in my heart: how happy it is to go to the mess hall after work! Home is really hell. And secretly I still complain to my wife: "You're tired because there are you and the child at home, not just for me. My grievance now is really indescribable. Without you and the child, I can barely get by financially. I don't even have to help cook after I've worked." Of course, this is my one-sided reason. On my wife's side, isn't she also full of tears with nowhere to shed them! Thinking like this, I immediately make a conclusion: poor people simply shouldn't have families, so they don't suffer while alive, and don't die with their eyes unclosed. But then I think: there are many poor people in the world, and very few rich people. If all poor people don't want families, won't humanity be extinct in a few years? Therefore, I feel that this is a fundamental and major problem in modern society.

The Practitioner of Saving the Nation Through Art 358

— Lin

Alleyway College Student

There is a special kind of person in Shanghai, namely, those who do not live in schools but live in the gatehouses or front buildings of alleyways on both sides of the road, living a "student life." Most of these people are unemployed and can be classified as vagrants. But because they were originally students, and haven't lost their "student demeanor" even though they now live in alleyways, some amusing people call them "alleyway college students."

Naturally, "alleyway college students" are mostly very "poor." But generally speaking, they all understand art very well, as can be proven by the arrangement of their houses. In their small gatehouse or front building, you can see an iron bed leaning diagonally in the corner of the room; a writing desk is also placed diagonally, facing the iron bed; next to the writing desk is inevitably a bookshelf, neatly arranged with some foreign books; the floor is

▲ Important text continues on page five ▲

Page 20

Page 21

scrubbed shiny; photos of movie stars are nailed to the most conspicuous place in the room; cooking utensils are inevitably placed in an inconspicuous place, because these things are not pretty; if they can still pawn a pair of pants, they must buy a bunch of fresh flowers to put in a vase, and when the breeze passes, you can smell a pleasant fragrance… In this way, although it is a small gatehouse or front building, after their "artistic" arrangement, it becomes very elegant.

"Alleyway college students" mostly cook their own meals, which is said to be based on hygiene. However, there is a difficulty here, namely, since they cook their own meals, they must buy their own groceries. Under the scrutiny of everyone, it is such a shameful thing to carry a grocery basket to buy groceries as a "college student"! This requires another clever solution. So, when the clever "alleyway college students" go to buy groceries, they don't carry a grocery basket, but secretly take a few newspapers to wrap the purchased groceries and bring them back. In this way, they are not afraid of being laughed at, because walking on the road carrying a package wrapped in a newspaper, no one can tell that this is someone returning from buying groceries. In buying groceries, they also have many "romantic anecdotes," such as telling jokes to the tofu-selling girl, touching other people's young mistresses, etc.; however, the most popular among them is that they often like to secretly touch the buttocks of "pretty" girls when people are crowded, which is said to relieve the monotonous life.

"Alleyway college students," like students studying in schools, besides reading books and writing articles from time to time, always like to hum a few lines of Peking Opera, play a few rounds of mahjong, or watch movies and gamble in their spare time. However, these are not their main characteristics. Their main characteristic is that they love to boast. They often get a little news from here and go there to boast; at the same time, they hear new news from there and come here to talk about it; no matter where, as long as they start bragging, they talk endlessly and wildly; they can brag from international politics to the life of a certain writer, to the eyes and thighs of a certain lady, to everything; if it were not for the need to eat and sleep, they could really finish bragging about all the problems of the universe and life, which of course has no time limit.

If you are happy and want to ask what the hopes of "alleyway college students" are, then I can tell you: they have many and great hopes. They hope for victory in the Anti-Japanese War, they hope for the success of the revolution,… but their most immediate hope is: that family or relatives and friends send money quickly, and that their lovers write letters!

Discourse on Occupations

Occupation and Occupational Interest 359

— Pang Chengqi

Man is a member of society, and occupation is a unit of social organization. The relationship between people and society is directly linked to the relationship between each occupation and people.

In a society, if every member has a considerable interest in his or her own occupation, then naturally he or she will work hard and pursue the occupation in which he or she can find interest. However, in the vortex of contradictions in the modern social system, it is not uncommon for an engineering graduate to be a clerk, or for an agriculturalist to be a history teacher... What is the reason for this? The simple answer is: to seek personal survival.

Most people treat occupation only as a means of livelihood. Here, livelihood means having enough to eat. The oppression of all material life and the threat of hunger force everyone to endure extreme pain in an occupational life that does not match their interests.

But everything should have a proper solution. We certainly cannot say that a person can pursue passionate dreams without eating, nor can we just wait for the world we need to arrive. Therefore, in this uninteresting, even detestable, occupation, there should be some practical remedies.

The best thing to do, of course, is to find an occupation that matches one's interests again, but this is absolutely impossible for most people. Therefore, the first thing we need to do is to examine our own occupation and see how it relates to society. If the relationship is close, even meaningful, then we must examine ourselves in detail and try to make our interests subordinate to the occupation for a meaningful cause, and learn in this environment, waiting for the useful days to come.

Conversely, if the occupation has no meaning to society, then, in order to avoid being eliminated in the future, we must learn other things in the possible scope outside of the occupation, strive according to our own interests, and prepare to run into a new life. Of course, for the sake of the present life, we cannot temporarily give up the occupation that we have no interest in, for the sake of life!

Let's end with two sentences: learn inside and outside of occupation, struggle in the circle of life!

Amateur Studies

A "Good People Government" Style of Good People School 360

— Jing Si

Just as the bread problem is about to be solved, unfortunately, because one has studied for a few years, a panic about the desire for knowledge arises again. Under the current economic system, these two problems are closely related to money. Therefore, poor fellows "cannot have both," and can only temporarily give up the latter for the former. However, "having obtained Shu, one desires Long" is a common human psychology. Food and clothing can solve physical hunger, but knowledge can heal spiritual hunger. Initially, I bought some books to look up and read, but as time went on, I felt that "studying alone without friends" leads to "doing twice the work for half the result." Moreover, specialized techniques such as arithmetic formulas must be taught by a teacher. Therefore, I longed for the school gates.

Balancing bread and education, I had to look for part-time night schools. However, I had no experience in finding schools and could only ask friends to help me find one. Eventually, I achieved my goal. According to the introducer, this is the best-known school in the city because it is "×-affiliated." Although the × character didn't shock me, I thought to myself, "Since it's the best-known, the professors must be well-learned scholars, right?" So I resolutely signed up.

Tuition fees, miscellaneous fees, lecture fees, report fees... all paid, and I was admitted to the school without encountering any difficulties. Paying "fees" for admission is the norm for all schools these days, isn't it? I thought.

Perhaps I am too naive? Why do others think it's normal, but I always feel something is wrong and can't help but be surprised.

The first impression that made me feel strange was the office staff preparing for the school opening, who were extraordinarily busy with student registration, enrollment, payment of fees, and so on, so that the school opening was delayed by two weeks. Three or four weeks after classes started, I received a mimeographed schedule, and we had to revise it repeatedly, so much so that we had to rewrite it ourselves. Under my hopeful belief at the time, I explained it this way: "This is the business of the office staff, fortunately, it has nothing to do with the teachers..."

But then came the second impression. The school's professors seemed to be too busy to be separated. Every night, there were two or three notices posted saying, "Mr. So-and-so is on leave due to ××, and the ×× class is temporarily suspended." The so-called temporary suspension is actually a permanent suspension. There were also temporary (?) incidents that were not notified to the academic affairs department, so it was common to encounter missing classes even without a leave notice. Experienced students, when faced with this kind of thing, would usually wait five minutes and then scatter like birds and beasts, wasting time, wasting transportation costs, and making a wasted trip... all of which were "commonplace" and not taken seriously. But, "Why are the professors so casual about teaching?" After careful inquiries, an old classmate explained to me: "What's so difficult to understand? Three and a half dollars per class, and deducted if you miss one! What's the big deal! And the school can save a few classes' worth of tuition!"

The professor, nicknamed "Good Person," walked into the classroom with a tofu-sized piece of paper in his right hand and a roll book under his left arm, always with a smile. He glanced at the whole room and began to call the roll, calling out "Miss Ter ×, Miss Ter ×..." This took three minutes. "Teacher, you called it wrong, she's Miss, not Miss Ter!" Little Zhang pointed to a female classmate and said. "Oh, I always forget, I must correct it next time." Then there was a burst of laughter. Then, from the weather to women's clothing, he spent another ten to twenty minutes before he began to copy the manuscript onto the blackboard. The characters were large and the board was small. After filling the entire blackboard, he would pause and wait for everyone to copy it into their notebooks before explaining it item by item. "It's true! What the teacher says always matches the written words exactly," one student said. "Oh..." This was the teacher's reply. But the teacher also knew that his time was lacking, so he pulled out some "Foreign countries are like this, I used to be like this in New York..." After class, I counted, a total of thirteen items were copied, one hundred and fifty or sixty words, and these copied outlines seemed to be imaginable even without reference books.

One day, after class, I gently said to "Good Person," "Teacher, why don't you give the prepared lectures to the academic affairs department for mimeographing and distribution? This way, everyone can save effort, and the teacher will have enough time to explain." "Don't you know? I also teach at some other schools, and I'm extremely busy... These lectures are all temporarily excerpted five minutes before class!" I admired his honesty and therefore forgave his difficulties, but I thought to myself, "Unfortunately, you have saved the school four dollars per person for lecture fees again."

"Good Person's" absences ranked first in the school. Statistics show that illness accounted for two-thirds of the reasons, and there were many laughable reasons for other incidents. Once, in class, students asked as usual: "Teacher, why didn't you come last time?" "Oh, I took the tram and was halfway there when a friend, Mr. So-and-so, said to me, 'Today is the ×× anniversary, why are you rushing to class?' I thought for a moment, 'Forget it,' and then..." "Why didn't you call the school? We were like 'idiots waiting for their wives'..." There was another burst of laughter. However, he never encountered student opposition or any strikes because he had two weapons. In addition to never getting angry, the most important thing was leniency during various exams.

Of course, there were more than just the above-mentioned things that made my belief in school drop from boiling point to freezing point. As someone who has never stepped into the gates of a university in my life, I couldn't help but be surprised, and I now believe that the university life described in novels is not entirely fictional.

Someone said, "Society is a university. You don't have to go to school to study, and you can only obtain true knowledge by throwing yourself into society." There is nothing wrong with that. I can only drop out of school and turn to society to work hard and explore. But, you must know that I do monotonous things every day for bread. The environment is simple and boring, and I deal with cunning merchants. What can you learn from that? Alas! Prosperous city, I now know that in your embrace, not only is bread difficult to find, but you cannot fully supply the emptiness of knowledge. You are just an embroidered pillow!

Part-time Correspondence Reading Group 361

— Xiao Jie

Nowadays, it is very difficult for store employees, especially apprentices like us, to acquire other knowledge in their spare time. We often encounter problems that we cannot explain when studying on our own, and there is simply no way to solve them. Previously, this magazine! Part-time Weekly! A certain gentleman proposed organizing a reading group, but its content cannot be suitable for our group of old-fashioned store apprentices; because old-fashioned store apprentices have no time to go out all year round except for a few days of the Lunar New Year. Under such circumstances, the proposal of "Part-time Correspondence Reading Group" was born.

Our method is to use the spirit of mutual assistance to conduct mutual research and exploration, and to answer questions by correspondence. In this way, we can not only increase our knowledge, but also make more friends, and even all apprentices are our closest friends.

The above is our proposal. As for all organizational regulations, they still need future members to express their opinions and discuss and formulate them. Those who wish to join, please send a letter to Tian Cheng Xiang Zhu Shop, No. 7 Xinbeimenkou, for transfer to Qian Xiaoxia, or to Hu Renling, Zhongxi Shanghao, No. 341 Guangxi Road, Nanjing Road.

Part-time Entertainment

Egg Suspended in Water 362

— Xie Xilin

丨One of the Scientific Games丨

This is a physically interesting trick. We can play it in our spare time. It costs nothing, and we can also get an important principle of physics from it. Now I will write it down below:

(1) Required items: one fresh egg, one tall and wide glass bottle, filled with clear water (cold water), and one bag of salt.

(2) Method: First, put the egg into the bottle. Because the egg is heavier than water, it sinks to the bottom of the bottle. Now, gradually add a little salt to the water, and stir the water at the same time to dissolve the salt evenly. When the salt is added to the appropriate amount, the egg will completely obey your command. You lift it up and place it in the center of the bottle. Just take your hand away, and it will still stand still. If you raise it or lower it again, it will also obey your orders and dare not move without permission.

(3) Reason: Because the specific gravity of the egg is greater than that of clear water, the egg sinks. Adding salt to the water turns the clear water into salt water. The specific gravity of salt water is greater than that of clear water. The more salt is added, the greater the specific gravity. When the specific gravity of salt water and clear water are equal, the egg will neither float nor sink, and will stay in the middle of the water. If you add more salt to make the specific gravity of the salt water greater than that of the egg, the egg will float on the water surface.

(4) Additional note: We know that east of the city of Jerusalem, there is a saltwater lake called the Dead Sea. The water there contains 25% salt, and its specific gravity is particularly large. No matter who goes there, they can swim safely.

Part-time Popular Stage, You Can Take a Seat at Any Time and Watch Everything Without Additional Fees

Lifesaver 363

— Li Ren

Characters: Police Officer, Undercover Agent, Unemployed Person, Spectators, Inspecting Officer, Another Police Officer.

Time: × Year × Month × Day, After New Year.

Location: Dockside.

Setting: In the center of the stage is a lamppost, on which hangs a rectangular glass cabinet, with the words "Lifesaver, Do Not Open Unless It Is An Emergency" written on the glass. Around it are piled some loading boxes. The undercover agent and the police officer appear together.

Undercover Agent: (To the police officer) Keep an eye on that side. There are a lot of people over there. It must be them. Damn it...

…　…Police Officer: (Looks around) Are they really going to fight? What about the foreigners? I really can't figure it out.

Undercover Agent: Humph, just wait and see. They are definitely going to have some kind of parade, shouting down something. Those stupid guys, there must be someone stirring up trouble inside. I don't believe in this so-called imperialism.

Police Officer: But...

Undercover Agent: "But" what? Are you going to go crazy with them?

Police Officer: That's not what I mean. I think they are really suffering too much. Didn't you hear them say yesterday that they paid the comprador 600 yuan in deposit to get a job as a fireman. Now that the comprador doesn't need them anymore, he's telling them to get lost. Is that reasonable?

Undercover Agent: That's just the fireman's fault. If it were me, I wouldn't have gotten that kind of job. How much is your salary per month?

Police Officer: Alas, it's not good, eight silver dollars, and I have to eat on my own. Recently, I'm still owed...

Undercover Agent: (Rather proudly) We get a regular salary of forty dollars, and there's a bonus for each case we handle; our bosses, I don't know how much more they get than us. (Suddenly whispers in the police officer's ear) That guy coming over there looks suspicious. You keep an eye on him, I'll go over there for a while and come back. (Saying this, he goes to the lower left) Maybe you'll have good luck.

Unemployed Person: (Appearing on stage in tattered clothes and a haggard appearance) Humph, (Speaking to himself) There's no business at the dock either... Yesterday, the day before yesterday, the day before the day before yesterday, a month, five months, it's been almost half a year since I had anything to do. I've been hungry for months, my wife, and her dog-raised little children. Alas, forget it, what's the point of living? (Walks to the riverside, stares for a while, the police officer is watching him strangely. After watching for a while, he turns around and looks around, preparing to lift his clothes and jump into the water)

Police Officer: (Coughs loudly)

Unemployed Person: (Startled by the police officer's cough, doesn't jump, turns around and takes a step or two, muttering in his mouth) The police are really the most hateful thing. When you want to live, they will beat you with a mourning stick; when you want to die, they will drag you back... (With a kind of nervous laugh) Hahahaha... (The laughter suddenly stops, he is already standing in front of the lamppost of the "Lifesaver", rubs his eyes, and looks at the words in surprise, slowly reading) Lifesaver, Do Not Open Unless It Is An Emergency! Ah, I'm saved! I'm saved! (As if crazy, shouting, he immediately raises his fist and hits the glass cabinet, with a loud bang, the glass breaks. At this time, the police officer has run behind him, grabs his collar and drags him, he takes two steps backward, his hand is cut by the glass, stained with blood.)

Police Officer: What are you doing? (The unemployed person is furious, thinking that he is going to grab his lifesaver, so he rushes towards the police officer, and the two of them twist into a ball, and people gradually gather to watch the fun. Finally, the unemployed person is pinned to the ground due to lack of strength, and the police officer blows his police whistle frantically. The previous undercover agent runs over)

Undercover Agent: (Saying to the police officer in a joking tone) You really got lucky. (Lifts his bloated "ham" and kicks the unemployed person hard) Damn you, dare you still stir up trouble?

Police Officer: (Stands aside, the unemployed person struggles to get up) It's not stirring up trouble, (Points to the lifesaver cabinet) It's hitting that thing. (The spectators laugh)

Undercover Agent: (Looking a little embarrassed) Ah, what? It's not stirring up trouble? (The inspecting officer comes with another police officer)

Inspecting Officer: What's the matter?

Police Officer: (Stands at attention, raises his hand) Report, this person broke the lifesaver and wanted to escape, I caught him.

Inspecting Officer: (Walks to the unemployed person) Why did you break that thing?

Unemployed Person: (Bluntly) I want to save my life!… (The inspecting officer and the rest of the people are startled)

Inspecting Officer: How can it save your life?

Unemployed Person: Isn't it written clearly on it? "Do Not Open Unless It Is An Emergency." I've been hungry for days, I haven't had a job for more than five months, I still have a wife and son, isn't that an emergency? (People laugh when they hear this) This police officer even wanted to grab mine.

Inspecting Officer: (Suppressing his laughter) You broke public property, and you dare to beat public officials, (To a police officer) Take him back to the station!

Unemployed Person: (Pitifully) I didn't commit a crime, sir, I want to save my own life!…

Inspecting Officer: (Gets angry) Go! Won't you go? (Slaps him. The unemployed person lowers his head and says nothing, and follows the police officer away. In the distance, there are shouts from the crowd: "Everyone go on the ship!" "We want our 600 yuan back!" The inspecting officer, the police officer, and the undercover agent rush to the place where the sound is coming from, the curtain closes.)
